  Capability-relevant (akceptowalne) — te technologie SĄ
  produktem/kapabilnością:
  - "MCP server", "MCP protocol", "MCP tools" — to IS the product
  - "Cloudflare Tunnel" — metoda dostępu (WHAT)

  - 02-wiedza/ — granica bezpieczeństwa (WHAT)
  - "PostgreSQL" — baza danych do integracji (WHAT)

● Przeprowadzam holistyczną ocenę jakości PRD...

  1. Document Flow & Coherence: Good

  PRD buduje narrację logicznie: wizja → sukces → żywe scenariusze użycia →
  wymogi domenowe → specyfikacja MCP → scoping z jasnymi granicami MVP →
  wymagania. Sekcja "What Makes This Special" w Executive Summary natychmiast
  wyjaśnia wartość i odróżnia od generycznego "mobile access to database".

  Mocne strony:
  - Żywe, konkretne user journeys w j. polskim ("10 minut w tramwaju") — nadają
  PRD autentyczność
  - Jasna granica MVP z explicit exclusions
  - Tabela Infrastructure Dependencies z mitigation strategy
  - Risk mitigation z fallbackami (np. Syncthing jeśli obsidian-headless
  zawiedzie)

  Słabsze strony:
  - FR15-18 mieszają constraints z capabilities
  - Brak sekcji error handling dla MCP tools
  - Pewien implementation leakage w wymaganiach

  2. Dual Audience:
  - Dla ludzi: Executive-friendly ✅, developer clarity ✅, stakeholder
  decision-making ✅
  - Dla LLM: Struktura ## ✅, FRs numerowane i testowalne ✅, MCP Tools
  Specification tables ✅, architecture readiness ✅, epic/story readiness ✅
  - Score: 4/5

● Świetne pytanie — i dotyka istoty problemu. Wyjaśnię, bo to zmienia
  rekomendację.

  ---
  Jak działa PRD — dwa modele

  Model 1: PRD jako "living document" (klasyczny)

  - Jeden PRD dla całego produktu, ciągle aktualizowany
  - Każda nowa funkcja, migracja, zmiana scope = update istniejącego PRD
  - PRD zawsze odzwierciedla aktualny stan zamierzony produktu
  - Tutaj implementation leakage jest poważnym problemem: każda zmiana stacku =
  update PRD

  Model 2: PRD jako "sprint/epic artifact" (BMad recommended)

  - Per sprint/epic — osobny PRD dla każdej większej inicjatywy
  - PRD opisuje INTENCJĘ i SCOPE w danym momencie czasu
  - Po dostarczeniu — PRD jest archiwizowany, nie aktualizowany
  - Następna inicjatywa = nowy PRD (z odwołaniem do poprzednich jeśli trzeba)

  ---
  A jak Ty to robisz?

  Zerknijmy na Twoją pracę:

  Listed 1 directory (ctrl+o to expand)

● Widzisz? Stosujesz Model 2 (per-sprint). Masz nawet konwencję w MEMORY:

  ▎ "Before editing PRD for a new sprint, ALWAYS copy current prd.md to _bmad-ou
  ▎ tput/planning-artifacts/archive/prd-sprint{N}-{short-name}-{date}.md"

  Czyli:
  - prd.md (aktualny) = sprint MCP server (ten, który walidujemy)
  - archive/prd-sprint9-sqlalchemy-orm-2026-04-10.md = poprzedni sprint
  - Następny sprint = archiwizacja tego PRD + nowy prd.md

  ---
  Co to oznacza dla pytania o migrację?

  Czy przy migracji zaglądasz do dawnych PRD?

  W praktyce: rzadko, ale czasem tak.

  Kiedy dawny PRD jest przydatny:
  - 🔍 Retrospektywa — "co właściwie planowaliśmy?" vs "co zrobiliśmy?"
  - 🔍 Onboarding — nowy człowiek (lub Ty po roku) chce zrozumieć dlaczego coś
  istnieje
  - 🔍 Forensics — "kiedy podjęliśmy decyzję X i dlaczego?"
  - 🔍 Migracja — sprawdzasz CO miało zostać dostarczone (intencja), żeby
  zaplanować jak to migrować

  Kiedy NIE przegląda się dawnych PRD:
  - 📐 Codzienna praca — patrzysz w kod, architecture.md, ADR-y
  - 📐 Małe zmiany — current state widać w kodzie
  - 📐 Decyzje techniczne — ADR-y są źródłem prawdy

  Konsekwencje dla Twojego PRD MCP

  PRD MCP server opisuje intencję dla TEGO sprintu: zbudować MCP server na NAS z
   Cloudflare Tunnel + obsidian-headless. Po dostarczeniu zostanie
  zarchiwizowany jako prd-sprint10-mcp-server-2026-04-XX.md.

  Jeśli za rok zrobisz migrację z obsidian-headless na coś innego:
  - ❌ NIE wrócisz do tego PRD żeby go aktualizować
  - ✅ Stworzysz nowy PRD "Sprint X — migracja sync mechanism" z nowym scope
  - ✅ Stary PRD pozostanie historycznym artefaktem mówiącym "tak myśleliśmy w
  2026-04"

  ---
  Wniosek — rewizja rekomendacji dla Change 8

  Skoro PRD to sprint artifact zamrożony w czasie, a nie living spec produktu:

  Implementation leakage ma znacznie mniejszy ciężar.

  Konkretność typu obsidian-headless, lenie-net, obsidian_note_versions jest
  wartością w sprint artifact:
  - Pokazuje DOKŁADNIE co planowano w tym momencie
  - Łatwiej zrozumieć retrospektywnie ("aha, użyli obsidian-headless")
  - Jeśli za rok zmienisz na Syncthing — to będzie nowy sprint i nowy PRD
  opisujący tę zmianę

  Nowa rekomendacja: Opcja B (zostawić jak jest) — z jedną drobną poprawką:
  - NFR7: zostawić obsidian_note_versions (już jest opisana wcześniej w sekcji
  "Note Version History" — to nie leakage, to spójność z resztą PRD)
  - NFR11, NFR12: zostawić — konkretność jest plus dla sprint artifact
  - NFR6: zostawić — Docker IS deployment dla tego sprintu

  Change 8 → SKIP (3 z 5 implementation leakage violations to false positives w
  kontekście sprint artifact)

  ---

  ---
  Propozycja scenariusza dla FR13

  Dla "User can view version history" — dodam edge case w Journey 1 (najmniej
  inwazyjne, naturalne miejsce):

  Propozycja (do dodania po obecnym Resolution Journey 1):

  ▎ Edge case — sprawdzenie historii zmian: Następnego dnia Ziutus otwiera 
  ▎ notatkę Kraje/Turcja/Polityka.md i widzi, że jakaś sekcja wygląda inaczej 
  ▎ niż pamięta. Pyta Claude'a: "pokaż mi co ostatnio zmieniłeś w tej notatce". 
  ▎ Claude wywołuje narzędzie historii wersji i pokazuje listę ostatnich zmian 
  ▎ (data, prompt który wywołał zmianę, diff). Ziutus widzi że to jego własna 
  ▎ instrukcja sprzed dwóch dni i spokojnie wraca do pracy.

  To uzasadnia FR13 + dodaje wartość: transparency + trust — użytkownik może
  sprawdzić co AI zrobiło z jego wiedzą.

  Wymaga też dodania nowego MCP tool obsidian_note_history w sekcji MCP Tools
  Specification (bo obecnie nie ma narzędzia żeby Claude mógł historię odczytać
  — jest tylko zapis do obsidian_note_versions).

      236 +MCP tools return structured errors with code, human-readable m
          +essage, and optional details. Claude surfaces these to the use
          +r conversationally.

      238 +| Error Code | Trigger | User-Facing Message Pattern |        
      239 +|------------|---------|------------------------------|       
      240 +| `article_not_found` | `lenie_get_article` / `lenie_delete_ar
          +ticle` with non-existent UUID | "Nie znalazłem artykułu o tym 
          +ID — możliwe że został wcześniej usunięty." |                 
      241 +| `note_not_found` | `obsidian_read_note` / `obsidian_note_his
          +tory` with non-existent path | "Nie ma notatki pod tą ścieżką 
          +w `02-wiedza/`." |                                            
      242 +| `note_path_invalid` | Path traversal attempt (`..`, absolute
          + path, outside `02-wiedza/`) | "Ścieżka jest poza dozwolonym o
          +bszarem `02-wiedza/`." (operacja odrzucona, próba zalogowana) 
          +|                                                             
      243 +| `vault_write_failed` | Filesystem error during `obsidian_wri
          +te_note` (permissions, disk full, sync conflict) | "Nie udało 
          +się zapisać notatki — sprawdź miejsce na dysku i status Obsidi
          +an Sync." |                                                   
      244 +| `database_unavailable` | PostgreSQL connection failure | "Ba
          +za Lenie jest niedostępna — sprawdź czy NAS i kontener `lenie-
          +ai-db` działają." |                                           
      245 +| `version_save_failed` | DB write to versioning store failed

          +m zapisać wersji historycznej. Notatka nie została zmieniona."
          + (NFR7 — no overwrite without version save) |

          +rs, and return shape |

          +ification) returns + [Note Version History](#note-version-hist
          +ory-mvp) | Field-level structure of responses and persisted re
          +cords |

          +or codes, triggers, and user-facing message patterns |        
      199 +| **Throughput & limits** | [Rate Limits & Concurrency](#rate-

          +miting in MVP |

      202 +

          +aking changes in tool signatures or error codes will be tracke

          +nector is assumed to be in lockstep with server deployment.

● Analizuję zrewidowany PRD pod kątem implikacji architektonicznych...

  ---
  Analysis Reflection

  Project: lenie-server-2025, Sprint 10 — MCP Server

  PRD definiuje 15 FRs zorganizowanych w 4 kategoriach (Article Discovery,
  Obsidian Note Management, Note Version History, Claude Integration) i 16 NFRs
  w 4 kategoriach (Performance, Security, Data Integrity, Integration).
  Klasyfikacja: api_backend / personal_ai_knowledge_management / medium
  complexity / brownfield.

  Key architectural aspects I notice

  Core funkcjonalność:
  - MCP server jako protocol adapter — nowy komponent pomiędzy Claude (mobile) a
   istniejącymi systemami (PostgreSQL na NAS + Obsidian vault filesystem)
  - 10 MCP tools (4 Lenie + 5 Obsidian + 1 history) eksponujących CRUD na
  artykułach i notatkach
  - Reuse istniejących DocumentService / SearchService — ale są obecnie
  sprzężone z Flask, wymaga decyzji o ekstrakcji

  Krytyczne NFRy kształtujące architekturę:
  - NFR5 (path traversal prevention) — wymaga walidacji ścieżek na każdej
  operacji filesystem
  - NFR9 (atomic versioning — version DB write przed file overwrite, no
  exceptions) — narzuca ordering: DB transaction → only then filesystem write
  - NFR7 (auth delegated to Cloudflare MCP Portal) — server jest auth-naive,
  brak własnego mechanizmu auth
  - NFR1-3 (response time targets <5s/<2s/<3s z measurement methods) — wymaga
  response logging
  - NFR13 (vault sync <60s przez obsidian-headless) — orkiestracja sync chain
  bez PC

  Unikalne wyzwania techniczne:
  - MCP protocol — nowy stack (Python SDK mcp), JSON-RPC over SSE/streamable
  HTTP
  - Cloudflare MCP Server Portal — Open Beta, ryzyko dostępności (fallback:
  simple tunnel + custom auth dokumentowany w risk mitigation)
  - obsidian-headless — Feb 2026 release, community Docker image (fallback:
  Syncthing)
  - Sync chain orchestration — MCP write → file → obsidian-headless → Obsidian
  Sync → devices

  Brownfield constraints:
  - Coexists z istniejącym 9-container NAS Docker stack
  - Reuses lenie-ai-db (PostgreSQL 18 + pgvector) na lenie-net network
  - New table obsidian_note_versions — Alembic migration
  - Nie zmienia AWS ingestion layer (API Gateway → SQS → DynamoDB) — out of
  scope

  Cross-cutting concerns

  1. Error handling pattern — 6 error codes (article_not_found, note_not_found,
  note_path_invalid, vault_write_failed, database_unavailable,
  version_save_failed), strukturowane responses, surfaced przez MCP do Claude
  konwersacyjnie
  2. Path validation — single source of truth dla 02-wiedza/ boundary (NFR5)
  3. Versioning ordering — atomic transaction wzór (DB write first, file write
  after)
  4. Configuration & secrets — env vars only (NFR6), nic w image
  5. Stability contract — tool names / param names / error codes są stabilne;
  nazwy tabel / sieci / kontenerów mogą się zmieniać (PRD API Documentation
  policy)

  Scale Indicators

  - Complexity: Medium (single user + fixed infrastructure, ale nowy protokół i
  nowa warstwa security)
  - Primary technical domain: API backend (MCP protocol adapter)
  - Estimated architectural components: 3 nowe (MCP server, obsidian-headless,
  Cloudflare Tunnel) + 1 nowa tabela DB
  - Cross-cutting: error handling, path security, atomic versioning,
  configuration

  ---
  Proponowana zawartość do dodania do architecture.md

  Dodaję jako nową sekcję ## Sprint 10 — Project Context Analysis (zgodnie z
  konwencją Sprint 4 / Sprint 6):

  ## Sprint 10 — Project Context Analysis

  ### Sprint Scope

  **Sprint name:** MCP Server — mobile knowledge workflow
  **PRD:** [_bmad-output/planning-artifacts/prd.md](prd.md) (revised 2026-04-12,
   validated 5/5 Excellent)
  **Goal:** Expose Lenie-AI knowledge base and Obsidian vault as Remote MCP
  server on NAS, accessible from Claude mobile (claude.ai Custom Connector).

  ### Requirements Overview

  **Functional Requirements (15 FRs across 4 capability areas):**

  - **Article Discovery & Review (FR1-FR5):** List unreviewed articles, fetch
  full content, search across title/content/note, delete, link notes to articles
   with review marking
  - **Obsidian Note Management (FR6-FR10):** CRUD on notes within `02-wiedza/`
  (read, create, overwrite, delete, list)
  - **Note Version History (FR11-FR13):** Auto-save before write, record
  prompt+before+after+article, retrieve history
  - **Claude Integration (FR14-FR15):** Custom Connector configuration, MCP tool
   invocation from mobile

  **Non-Functional Requirements (16 NFRs across 4 quality areas):**

  - **Performance (NFR1-NFR3):** Response time targets (5s/2s/3s) with
  measurement via response logging
  - **Security (NFR4-NFR8):** HTTPS via Cloudflare Tunnel, path traversal
  prevention, no secrets in image, OAuth via Cloudflare Portal, no direct port
  exposure
  - **Data Integrity (NFR9-NFR11):** Mandatory version-before-overwrite, atomic
  DB transactions, indefinite version retention
  - **Integration (NFR12-NFR16):** MCP protocol compatibility, vault sync <60s,
  NAS-driven sync chain, Obsidian Sync continuous, PostgreSQL connection on
  existing network

  **Scale & Complexity:**

  - **Primary domain:** API backend (specifically: MCP protocol adapter)
  - **Complexity level:** Medium — single user + brownfield + fixed
  infrastructure, but introduces new protocol stack and security layer
  - **Estimated new architectural components:** 3 containers (MCP server,
  obsidian-headless, Cloudflare Tunnel client) + 1 new database table

  ### Technical Constraints & Dependencies

  **Hardware:**
  - NAS: QNAP TS-453Be (modest CPU/RAM, Docker host)
  - Coexistence with existing 9-container NAS Docker stack (must not disrupt)

  **External services in scope:**
  - Cloudflare DNS + Tunnel + MCP Server Portal (Zero Trust OAuth) — new
  - Obsidian Sync (Standard plan, valid until 2026-11-02) — existing
  subscription
  - claude.ai Custom Connector — entry point

  **Brownfield reuse requirements:**
  - `lenie-ai-db` (PostgreSQL 18 + pgvector) on `lenie-net` Docker network —
  existing
  - `DocumentService` / `SearchService` from `library/` — currently coupled to
  Flask, requires extraction decision
  - Existing Alembic migration system for new `obsidian_note_versions` table

  **New stack additions:**
  - Python `mcp` SDK (JSON-RPC over SSE/streamable HTTP)
  - `obsidian-headless` container (community Docker image, Feb 2026 release)
  - Cloudflare client (`cloudflared`) for tunnel

  **Maturity risks (with PRD-documented fallbacks):**
  - MCP protocol (new) — mitigated by official Python SDK + community examples
  - Cloudflare MCP Portal (Open Beta) — fallback: simple tunnel + custom auth
  header
  - obsidian-headless (Feb 2026) — fallback: Syncthing migration

  ### Cross-Cutting Concerns Identified

  1. **Structured error handling** — 6 error codes from PRD must be implemented
  as a single source of truth (probably an enum + response envelope) so Claude
  can surface them conversationally
  2. **Path security boundary** — `02-wiedza/` enforcement must be a single,
  audited utility called by every Obsidian tool (not duplicated per tool)
  3. **Atomic versioning ordering** — DB version write must succeed before file
  overwrite; failure mode (`version_save_failed`) explicitly cancels write —
  implies transaction-like coordinator pattern
  4. **Configuration & secrets management** — leverages existing
  `unified_config_loader` (Vault/AWS/env backends); MCP server must not bake any
   secrets into image
  5. **Stability contract enforcement** — tool names / param names / error codes
   are the public API surface (per PRD API Documentation);
  table/network/container names are internal and may change without API version
  bump
  6. **Service decoupling for reuse** — `DocumentService` / `SearchService` must
   be Flask-independent (likely already mostly there per PRD's "already
  decoupled" note, but needs verification)
  7. **Sync chain reliability** — file-write → obsidian-headless detects →
  Obsidian Sync → devices; failure at any link silently degrades user experience
   without alerting (monitoring is post-MVP)

  ---
  What would you like to do?

  [A] Advanced Elicitation — pogłębimy implikacje architektoniczne (np. service
  decoupling strategy, sync chain failure modes)
  [P] Party Mode — różne perspektywy (np. SRE, security, MCP protocol expert)
  [C] Continue — zapisuję analysis i przechodzę do Step 3 (Starter Template
  Evaluation — w naszym przypadku raczej "stack & framework decisions")

● Step 3 to "Starter Template Evaluation" — w naszym brownfield projekcie to
  bardziej "do we adopt a scaffolding template or follow existing project
  patterns?". Sprawdzam aktualny stan MCP SDK dla Pythona:

● context7 - resolve-library-id (MCP)(libraryName: "MCP Python SDK", query:
                                     "Python MCP server SDK for building Model
                                     Context Protocol servers, current project
                                     scaffolding, FastMCP")

● context7 - query-docs (MCP)(libraryId: "/modelcontextprotocol/python-sdk",
                             query: "Getting started scaffolding create new MCP
                             server project, FastMCP quickstart, recommended
                             project structure, streamable HTTP transport")
● Mam potrzebne info z Context7. MCP Python SDK v1.12.4 to oficjalny pakiet od
  modelcontextprotocol org, z high-level FastMCP API. Prezentuję analizę:

  ---
  Starter Template Evaluation — Sprint 10

  Primary Technology Domain

  API backend (MCP protocol adapter) — nie klasyczna web aplikacja/backend.
  Specyficzny stack:

  - Python 3.11 (zgodnie z całym projektem)
  - mcp SDK (official Anthropic/modelcontextprotocol package, v1.12.4)
  - FastMCP high-level API — decorator-based (@mcp.tool())
  - Streamable HTTP transport (recommended for production per SDK docs)

  Starter Options Considered

  Option: create-mcp-server CLI scaffolding
  Verdict: ❌ Reject
  Rationale: Nie istnieje dla Pythona jako oficjalne CLI (w przeciwieństwie do
    Node ekosystemu). SDK dostarcza examples, nie scaffolding.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: External Python starter (cookiecutter, kopier)
  Verdict: ❌ Reject
  Rationale: Brownfield project ma ustalone konwencje (uv, pyproject, ruff,
    pytest, library/ services) — zewnętrzne scaffolding wymusiłoby conflict z
    tymi konwencjami
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: Fork/copy examples/servers/simple-tool z MCP SDK repo
  Verdict: ⚠️ Partial
  Rationale: Dobre jako referencja, ale to gotowy projekt — kopiowanie struktury

    = duplikacja konwencji
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Option: fastmcp high-level API w SDK + existing project conventions
  Verdict: ✅ Selected
  Rationale: Minimalne dependencies, decorator-based tool registration pasuje do

    clean tool definitions z PRD, integruje się z istniejącym pyproject.toml/uv
    workflow

  Selected Approach: No external starter — extend existing project conventions

  Rationale for Selection:

  1. Brownfield hygiene — Twój projekt ma dojrzałe konwencje (backend/library/
  dla serwisów, backend/tests/unit/ + tests/integration/, Alembic migrations, uv
   deps, ruff/pytest tooling). Zewnętrzny starter wymusiłby duplikację lub
  conflict.
  2. MCP SDK to biblioteka, nie framework — nie potrzebuje scaffolding. FastMCP
  instance + decorators + transport = kompletny serwer w pojedynczym pliku.
  3. Transport: Streamable HTTP stateless + JSON responses — SDK docs explicitly
   rekomendują to dla produkcji. Pasuje do Cloudflare Tunnel behind OAuth (każdy
   request niezależny, skaluje się prosto).
  4. Deploy: Docker container following existing compose.nas.yaml pattern.

  Initialization (Implementation Story 1)

  Nie ma "CLI command do uruchomienia" — to brownfield extension. Pierwsza
  implementation story polega na:

  # 1. Create new backend subdirectory for MCP server
  mkdir -p backend/mcp_server/{tools,tests}

  # 2. Add MCP SDK to dependencies
  cd backend && uv add mcp

  # 3. Sync WSL venv (per project convention from CLAUDE.md)
  wsl bash -c "... uv sync --python .venv_wsl/bin/python --active"

  # 4. Create Docker service in compose.nas.yaml
  # 5. Implement stateless HTTP server skeleton with mcp SDK

  Architectural Decisions Provided by Selected Approach

  Language & Runtime:
  - Python 3.11 (project-wide standard)
  - mcp SDK v1.12.4+ as primary framework
  - uv for dependency management (project convention)

  Entry point pattern:
  - FastMCP instance with decorator-registered tools
  - stateless_http=True, json_response=True for production HTTP mode
  - mcp.run(transport="streamable-http") as launch command

  Project Structure (within backend/):
  backend/mcp_server/
  ├── __init__.py
  ├── main.py                    # FastMCP instance, entry point, transport
  config
  ├── tools/
  │   ├── __init__.py
  │   ├── lenie.py               # 4 Lenie tools (unreviewed_articles, get,
  search, delete)
  │   ├── obsidian.py            # 5 Obsidian tools (read, write, list, delete,
  history)
  │   └── _common.py             # path validation, error response envelope
  ├── errors.py                  # Error enum + response envelope (cross-cutting
   concern #1)
  ├── path_security.py           # 02-wiedza/ boundary enforcer (cross-cutting
  #2)
  └── tests/
      ├── unit/                  # tool logic, path validation, error mapping
      └── integration/           # end-to-end with real PG + tmp vault

  Services reuse:
  - Import DocumentService / SearchService z backend/library/ (zgodnie z PRD
  "already decoupled")
  - Weryfikacja Flask-independence (FR/NFR check) przed implementacją tools

  Testing:
  - pytest (już w projekcie)
  - Unit tests per tool: path validation, error mapping, service invocation
  - Integration tests against real PostgreSQL (NAS or Docker per CLAUDE.md
  memory — use NAS database for DB changes)

  Deployment:
  - New Docker service in infra/docker/compose.nas.yaml
  - Connected to existing lenie-net network (for lenie-ai-db)
  - Volume-mounted vault at {OBSIDIAN_VAULT_PATH}/02-wiedza/
  - Env vars only for secrets (via existing unified_config_loader)

  Note: Project initialization (directory + dependencies + Docker service
  skeleton) should be the first implementation story, before any tool logic.

  ---
  A/P/C Menu

  [A] Advanced Elicitation — pogłębić alternatywy (np. "fastapi + uvicorn direct
   zamiast mcp.run()"?)
  [P] Party Mode — perspektywy (SRE view na deployment, security review na
  transport)
  [C] Continue — zapisuję do architecture.md i idę do Step 4 (Core Architectural
   Decisions — tu decydujemy o service decoupling, error envelope struct, path
  security pattern)

● Zapisane. Step 4 — Core Architectural Decisions:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Step 4 — Core Architectural Decisions. Przeglądam co jest już zdecydowane i co
   wymaga decyzji dla Sprint 10.

  Już zdecydowane (nie re-decydujemy)

  - Language/Runtime: Python 3.11, uv — project standard
  - Framework: mcp SDK v1.12.4+ z FastMCP API — Step 3
  - Transport: Streamable HTTP stateless + JSON responses — Step 3
  - Database: PostgreSQL 18 + pgvector (lenie-ai-db) — istniejąca infrastruktura
  - ORM: SQLAlchemy 2.0 — per Sprint 9 migration (jest już w projekcie)
  - Auth layer: Cloudflare Zero Trust OAuth (network-level) — PRD decision
  - Secrets: env vars via unified_config_loader (Vault/AWS/env) — project
  convention
  - Testing: pytest z istniejącą strukturą — project convention
  - Deployment: Docker on NAS (compose.nas.yaml) — existing pattern

  ---
  Critical Decisions do podjęcia (Sprint 10)

  Category 1: Data Architecture

  D1 — obsidian_note_versions table — SQLAlchemy model + Alembic migration

  Schema z PRD jest jasny. Decyzja: SQLAlchemy ORM model w 
  backend/library/db/models.py (spójnie z resztą po Sprint 9 migration). Alembic
   migration jako drugi story.
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ akceptujemy bez debaty

  D2 — Transactional ordering (NFR9: DB write PRZED file overwrite)

  Problem: nie ma natywnej "atomic transaction" pokrywającej DB + filesystem.
  Potrzebny pattern coordinator.

  Opcje:
  - A. Try-DB-first, then-file (imperative): zapisz version do DB → commit →
  dopiero wtedy nadpisz plik. Jeśli file write fail, version w DB to "orphan
  record" (nieszkodliwy, to tylko snapshot).
  - B. Two-phase commit (overkill): saga pattern z compensating actions
  - C. File write first, DB second: ❌ narusza NFR9

  Rekomendacja: Opcja A — najprostsza, NFR9 compliant, orphan version records są
   OK (jeśli kiedyś file write się nie udał, history pokazuje "attempted
  change"). Loguj orphans do późniejszej analizy.

  D3 — Version retention (NFR11: indefinite)

  Decyzja: żadnej automatic purging w MVP. Partition table może wejść w Phase 2
  jeśli rozmiar będzie problemem. Single user = realistycznie <10k wersji w rok.
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ akceptujemy

  ---
  Category 2: Security

  D4 — Path traversal prevention (NFR5)

  Opcje:
  - A. pathlib.Path.resolve() + prefix check: standard Python, bezpieczne gdy
  poprawnie użyte (resolve follows symlinks!)
  - B. Custom validator z explicit character blocklist
  - C. os.path.commonpath() check

  Rekomendacja: Opcja A — resolve(strict=False) + .is_relative_to(vault_root)
  (Python 3.9+). Jeden helper path_security.ensure_within_vault(path) -> Path
  wywoływany przez KAŻDE Obsidian tool (cross-cutting concern #2). Test
  coverage: dedicated unit tests dla .., absolute paths, symlinks, unicode edge
  cases.

  D5 — MCP server auth stance

  Auth jest w Cloudflare. MCP server sam z siebie jest auth-blind. Decyzja:
  trust upstream, bez walidacji nagłówków (MCP Portal dodaje
  Cf-Access-Jwt-Assertion i Cf-Access-Authenticated-User-Email — logujemy user
  email dla audit trail, ale NIE weryfikujemy JWT).

  Uwaga security: zakładamy że MCP server NIGDY nie jest eksponowany direct
  (NFR8). Dokumentujemy to jako explicit security assumption.
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ trust upstream + log user email

  ---
  Category 3: API & Communication

  D6 — Error response envelope

  MCP protocol ma własny error format (JSON-RPC errors). Decyzja:
  - A. Use native MCP errors — każdy tool rzuca McpError(code=..., message=...)
  z mapowaniem na nasze 6 error codes
  - B. Custom wrapper nad successful responses z {ok: bool, error: {...}}

  Rekomendacja: Opcja A — native MCP errors. SDK ma McpError class, Claude
  Custom Connector wie jak je parsować. Stworzymy backend/mcp_server/errors.py z
   6 naszymi error codes jako Enum + helper raise_article_not_found() itp.
  Mapping na JSON-RPC error codes (-32000 to -32099 reserved for server errors).

  D7 — Tool parameter validation

  FastMCP używa type hints + Pydantic automatically. Decyzja: użyj natywnego 
  Pydantic z FastMCP (annotacje typów na funkcji tool = auto-validation).
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ akceptujemy (zero extra code)

  ---
  Category 4: Integration / Service Reuse

  D8 — Service reuse pattern dla DocumentService/SearchService

  PRD mówi "already decoupled from Flask" — ale weryfikacja required. Opcje:
  - A. Direct import jeśli services są Flask-free: from library.services import 
  DocumentService
  - B. Extract to new package backend/library/services/ jeśli jest coupling
  - C. Thin adapter w mcp_server/adapters.py który ukrywa różnice

  Rekomendacja: Opcja A z weryfikacją — pierwsza implementation story zawiera
  acceptance criterion "verify DocumentService/SearchService importable without
  Flask app context". Jeśli nie — zostaje Opcja B jako refactor story. Unikamy
  Opcji C (niepotrzebna warstwa).

  D9 — obsidian_note_history query pattern

  Decyzja: SQLAlchemy query na obsidian_note_versions WHERE note_path=X ORDER BY
   created_at DESC LIMIT 10 (default). Zwraca: date, user_prompt, unified diff
  (content_before vs content_after — generowany przez difflib.unified_diff()
  server-side).
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ akceptujemy z jedną uwagą — diff generation server-side
  unika przesyłania pełnych treści przez MCP (oszczędność ruchu dla dużych
  notatek)

  ---
  Category 5: Infrastructure

  D10 — Cloudflared deployment pattern

  Opcje:
  - A. Sidecar w compose — osobny kontener, network_mode: service:mcp-server lub
   shared network
  - B. Runs on NAS directly (nie w Docker) — systemd service
  - C. Embedded — w tym samym kontenerze co MCP server

  Rekomendacja: Opcja A — sidecar kontener cloudflared w compose.nas.yaml,
  connected do lenie-net, route do mcp-server:port. Oddzielne responsibility,
  łatwe restarty, konfiguracja przez env/mount. Matches Cloudflare's recommended
   pattern.

  D11 — obsidian-headless — which image

  PRD linkuje https://github.com/Belphemur/obsidian-headless-sync-docker.

  Decyzja: lock to specific image tag w Sprint 10 (np.
  belphemur/obsidian-headless-sync:v1.0.0 — konkretny tag, nie :latest). Jeśli
  community image przestanie być maintained, PRD-documented fallback =
  Syncthing.
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ pinned tag + risk monitoring

  D12 — Health check / liveness

  MVP: NFR1-3 measurement przez response logging (Step 2 content). Dodatkowo:
  MCP server exposes /healthz HTTP endpoint (simple 200 OK) dla Docker health
  check. To nie jest MCP tool, to plain HTTP route w tym samym serverze —
  FastMCP pozwala dodać raw routes via underlying Starlette app.
  - Rekomendacja: ✅ akceptujemy (minimal cost, Docker healthcheck = automatic
  restart on stuck server)

  ---
  Proponowana treść do architecture.md

  Poniżej struktura, którą dodam jako ## Sprint 10 — Core Architectural 
  Decisions:

  Decision summary table: 12 decisions (D1-D12) pogrupowanych w 5 kategorii,
  każda z: decision, rationale, affects (FR/NFR/components), status
  (selected/deferred).

  Cascading implications noted:
  - D2 (ordering) + D6 (error envelope) → version_save_failed error code wymaga
  specific coordinator logic
  - D4 (path security) + D6 (error envelope) → note_path_invalid jest raised
  przez path_security.ensure_within_vault()
  - D8 (service reuse) → może wygenerować extra story "refactor library/services
   Flask-independent" jeśli weryfikacja pokaże coupling

  ---
  A/P/C Menu

  [A] Advanced Elicitation — pogłębić konkretne decyzję (np. D2 orchestration
  edge cases, D8 service decoupling strategy)
  [P] Party Mode — multi-perspective (np. SRE on D10 tunnel deployment, security
   review on D5)
  [C] Continue — akceptuję wszystkie 12 decyzji, zapisuję do architecture.md,
  idę do Step 5 (Implementation Patterns)

  Czy jest jakaś konkretna decyzja która wymaga dyskusji zanim zatwierdzimy?
  Jeśli nie — C.

      2260 +                                                             
      2261 +**D1 — `obsidian_note_versions` table: SQLAlchemy ORM model +
           + Alembic migration**                                         
      2262 +                                                             
      2263 +- **Decision:** Define model in `backend/library/db/models.py
           +` alongside existing models (post-Sprint 9 convention). Schem
           +a per PRD (id, note_path, content_before, content_after, user
           +_prompt, article_id FK, changed_by, created_at).             
      2264 +- **Rationale:** Consistent with post-Sprint 9 SQLAlchemy ORM
           + adoption. Alembic handles schema evolution. No raw SQL in to
           +ol code.                                                     
      2265 +- **Affects:** FR11, FR12, FR13, NFR9, NFR10, NFR11 — all ver
           +sion history functionality                                   
      2266 +- **Migration story:** Dedicated implementation story for Ale
           +mbic migration, before any tool that writes versions         
      2267 +                                                             
      2268 +**D2 — Transactional ordering: DB-first, then filesystem (Opt
           +ion A)**                                                     
      2269 +                                                             
      2270 +- **Decision:** `obsidian_write_note` sequence: (1) BEGIN DB 
           +transaction → (2) INSERT version record → (3) COMMIT → (4) ov
           +erwrite file. If step 4 fails, raise `vault_write_failed` — v
           +ersion record stays in DB as "attempted change" (orphan).    
      2271 +- **Rationale:** Simplest pattern satisfying NFR9 (no overwri
           +te without version save). Orphan records are harmless (repres
           +ent attempted writes, useful for audit/debugging). Two-phase 
           +commit would be overkill for single-user system with low writ
           +e volume.                                                    
      2272 +- **Affects:** NFR9, FR8 (overwrite), FR11 (auto-save), error
           + codes `version_save_failed` and `vault_write_failed`        
      2273 +- **Implementation note:** Log orphan detection as WARNING (f
           +ile mtime < latest version.created_at for same path indicates
           + failed overwrite)                                           
      2274 +- **Cascading implication:** Error code `version_save_failed`
           + must abort the whole operation before any file touch        
      2275 +                                                             
      2276 +**D3 — Version retention: indefinite, no automatic purging in
           + MVP**                                                       
      2277 +                                                             
      2278 +- **Decision:** Per NFR11 — keep all versions forever in MVP.
           + No partition, no TTL, no pruning job.                       
      2279 +- **Rationale:** Single user, realistic <10k versions/year. T
           +able partitioning or pruning can be added in Phase 2 if size 
           +becomes a concern. Keeps MVP simple.                         
      2280 +- **Affects:** NFR11 only                                    
      2281 +                                                             
      2282 +### Authentication & Security                                
      2283 +                                                             
      2284 +**D4 — Path traversal prevention: `pathlib.Path.resolve()` + 
           +`.is_relative_to()`**                                        
      2285 +                                                             
      2286 +- **Decision:** Single helper `path_security.ensure_within_va
           +ult(relative_path: str) -> Path` called by EVERY Obsidian too
           +l before any filesystem access. Uses `Path.resolve(strict=Fal
           +se)` then `resolved.is_relative_to(VAULT_ROOT / "02-wiedza")`
           + (Python 3.9+).                                              
      2287 +- **Rationale:** `resolve()` follows symlinks and normalizes 
           +`..`, catching traversal attempts after path normalization. `
           +is_relative_to()` is stdlib, explicit, and testable. Single s
           +ource of truth satisfies cross-cutting concern #2.           
      2288 +- **Affects:** NFR5, all Obsidian tools (FR6-FR10, FR13)     
      2289 +- **Test coverage required:** `..` traversal, absolute paths,
           + symlink escape, unicode edge cases, null bytes              
      2290 +- **Cascading implication:** `note_path_invalid` error code r
           +aised exclusively by this helper                             
      2291 +                                                             
      2292 +**D5 — MCP server auth stance: trust upstream, log user ident
           +ity**                                                        
      2293 +                                                             
      2294 +- **Decision:** MCP server is auth-blind. Relies on Cloudflar
           +e MCP Portal to reject unauthenticated requests upstream. Log
           +s `Cf-Access-Authenticated-User-Email` header value (if prese
           +nt) for audit trail, but does NOT verify the `Cf-Access-Jwt-A
           +ssertion` JWT.                                               
      2295 +- **Rationale:** Defense-in-depth token validation is explici
           +tly out of MVP (per PRD). Single-user system — identity is in
           +formational, not authorizational. NFR8 (no direct port exposu
           +re) is the primary security boundary.                        
      2296 +- **Affects:** NFR7, NFR8, audit logging approach            
      2297 +- **Explicit security assumption (must be documented in deplo
           +yment runbook):** MCP server port MUST NEVER be exposed beyon
           +d `lenie-net` Docker network. If Cloudflare Tunnel fails, ser
           +ver becomes unreachable (fail-closed), not unauthenticated-op
           +en.                                                          
      2298 +                                                             
      2299 +### API & Communication                                      
      2300 +                                                             
      2301 +**D6 — Error response envelope: native MCP protocol errors (J
           +SON-RPC)**                                                   
      2302 +                                                             
      2303 +- **Decision:** Use `mcp.McpError` class from SDK. Create `ba
           +ckend/mcp_server/errors.py` with 6 error codes as Enum + help
           +er functions (`raise_article_not_found(uuid)`, `raise_note_no
           +t_found(path)`, etc.). Each helper raises `McpError` with a J
           +SON-RPC error code in the `-32000 to -32099` server-reserved 
           +range and a human-readable message matching PRD's user-facing
           + pattern.                                                    
      2304 +- **Rationale:** Claude Custom Connector natively parses JSON
           +-RPC errors. No extra wrapping needed. Single source of truth
           + for error codes matches cross-cutting concern #1.           
      2305 +- **Affects:** All 6 PRD error codes (`article_not_found`, `n
           +ote_not_found`, `note_path_invalid`, `vault_write_failed`, `d
           +atabase_unavailable`, `version_save_failed`), all tools      
      2306 +- **Cascading implication:** Error code ↔ JSON-RPC code mappi
           +ng is frozen in `errors.py` (part of stability contract per P
           +RD API Documentation)                                        
      2307 +                                                             
      2308 +**D7 — Tool parameter validation: native FastMCP Pydantic**  
      2309 +                                                             
      2310 +- **Decision:** Use Python type hints on tool function signat
           +ures; FastMCP auto-generates Pydantic validators. No manual v
           +alidation code.                                              
      2311 +- **Rationale:** Zero extra code, consistent with FastMCP idi
           +oms, type hints double as documentation. Complex validation (
           +e.g., UUID format) via Pydantic `Field(pattern=...)` or custo
           +m validators as needed.                                      
      2312 +- **Affects:** All 10 MCP tools                              
      2313 +- **Limitation:** Custom error messages for validation failur
           +es are Pydantic defaults — acceptable for MVP, can be customi
           +zed later                                                    
      2314 +                                                             
      2315 +### Integration / Service Reuse                              
      2316 +                                                             
      2317 +**D8 — Service reuse: direct import from `backend/library/`, 
           +verified Flask-independence**                                
      2318 +                                                             
      2319 +- **Decision:** Import `DocumentService`, `SearchService` dir
           +ectly in MCP tool modules. First implementation story include
           +s acceptance criterion: "verify service imports and basic inv
           +ocation work without Flask app context active."              
      2320 +- **Rationale:** PRD asserts services are "already decoupled 
           +from Flask." If verification fails, escalate to a refactor st
           +ory (B — extract to cleaner package). Avoids premature adapte
           +r layer (C) unless actual coupling is discovered.            
      2321 +- **Affects:** All Lenie tools (FR1-FR4)                     
      2322 +- **Risk:** Discovery of hidden Flask coupling (e.g., `curren
           +t_app`, `request` globals used inside services) — mitigated b
           +y explicit verification step                                 
      2323 +- **Cascading implication:** May generate additional refactor
           + story if coupling found                                     
      2324 +                                                             
      2325 +**D9 — `obsidian_note_history` query pattern: SQLAlchemy quer
           +y with server-side diff generation**                         
      2326 +                                                             
      2327 +- **Decision:** `SELECT * FROM obsidian_note_versions WHERE n
           +ote_path=:path ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT :limit` (defaul
           +t 10). Generate unified diff on the server using `difflib.uni
           +fied_diff()` from `content_before` vs `content_after`. Return
           +: list of `{date, user_prompt, diff, article_id}` — NOT full 
           +content.                                                     
      2328 +- **Rationale:** Server-side diff generation avoids shipping 
           +full note contents over MCP for every history lookup (can be 
           +tens of KB per version for long notes). Diff is much smaller 
           +and more immediately useful to the user. Full content remains
           + accessible via separate query if needed.                    
      2329 +- **Affects:** FR13, new tool `obsidian_note_history`        
      2330 +- **Payload estimate:** ~2-5 KB per version vs 10-50 KB if re
           +turning full content                                         
      2331 +                                                             
      2332 +### Infrastructure & Deployment                              
      2333 +                                                             
      2334 +**D10 — `cloudflared` tunnel: sidecar container in `compose.n
           +as.yaml`**                                                   
      2335 +                                                             
      2336 +- **Decision:** Separate container `cloudflared` in `compose.
           +nas.yaml`, connected to `lenie-net`, routing public traffic t
           +o `mcp-server:<port>`. Config via token in env var (mounted f
           +rom `unified_config_loader`).                                
      2337 +- **Rationale:** Matches Cloudflare's official recommended pa
           +ttern. Separate responsibility (tunnel lifecycle vs MCP logic
           +). Restart of one doesn't affect the other. Clear observabili
           +ty (logs per container).                                     
      2338 +- **Affects:** NFR4, NFR8                                    
      2339 +- **Alternative rejected:** Running `cloudflared` on NAS host
           + directly (Option B) — couples to NAS OS, harder to reproduce
           + in non-prod environments                                    
      2340 +                                                             
      2341 +**D11 — `obsidian-headless` image: pinned tag from community 
           +repository**                                                 
      2342 +                                                             
      2343 +- **Decision:** Use [`Belphemur/obsidian-headless-sync-docker
           +`](https://github.com/Belphemur/obsidian-headless-sync-docker
           +) with a pinned version tag (e.g., `v1.0.0` or latest stable 
           +semver at implementation time). Never use `:latest` tag. Docu
           +ment tag choice + release date in `compose.nas.yaml` comment.
      2344 +- **Rationale:** Community image from new project (Feb 2026).
           + Pinning prevents silent breakage from upstream changes. Upgr
           +ade is an explicit PR. Fallback path (Syncthing migration) do
           +cumented in PRD risk mitigation.                             
      2345 +- **Affects:** NFR13, NFR14, NFR15 (sync chain)              
      2346 +- **Risk monitoring:** Check repository activity monthly; if 
           +unmaintained, trigger Syncthing fallback evaluation before Ob
           +sidian Sync subscription expires (2026-11-02)                
      2347 +                                                             
      2348 +**D12 — Health check: HTTP `/healthz` endpoint alongside MCP 
           +tools**                                                      
      2349 +                                                             
      2350 +- **Decision:** Expose plain HTTP `GET /healthz` returning `2
           +00 OK` (no auth required, routed BEFORE OAuth gate via Cloudf
           +lare bypass rule OR exposed on separate internal port). FastM
           +CP uses Starlette internally — add a raw route via the underl
           +ying app.                                                    
      2351 +- **Rationale:** Enables Docker `healthcheck:` directive → au
           +tomatic container restart on hung process. Minimal implementa
           +tion cost. Not an MCP tool (doesn't require Claude invocation
           +).                                                           
      2352 +- **Affects:** Deployment resilience; no PRD requirement but 
           +directly supports NFR1-3 (performance via auto-recovery)     
      2353 +- **Implementation note:** `/healthz` is NOT part of the MCP 
           +API surface — it's an operational endpoint. Documented in dep
           +loyment runbook, not in PRD API Documentation.               
      2354 +                                                             
      2355 +### Decision Impact Analysis                                 
      2356 +                                                             
      2357 +**Implementation Sequence (recommended story ordering):**    
      2358 +                                                             
      2359 +1. **Project initialization** — `backend/mcp_server/` skeleto
           +n, `uv add mcp`, Docker service placeholder (before any logic
           +)                                                            
      2360 +2. **Service reuse verification** (D8) — validates PRD assump
           +tion; may fork into refactor story if coupling found         
      2361 +3. **Alembic migration for `obsidian_note_versions`** (D1)   
      2362 +4. **Error module + enum** (D6) — `backend/mcp_server/errors.
           +py`                                                          
      2363 +5. **Path security helper** (D4) — `backend/mcp_server/path_s
           +ecurity.py` with exhaustive tests                            
      2364 +6. **Lenie tools** (FR1-FR4) — simpler, no filesystem        
      2365 +7. **Obsidian read-only tools** (FR6, FR10) — uses D4        
      2366 +8. **Obsidian write tools** (FR7, FR8, FR9) — uses D2 coordin
           +ator pattern                                                 
      2367 +9. **Note history tool** (FR13) — uses D9 query + diff       
      2368 +10. **Review-mark logic** (FR5) — tied to `obsidian_write_not
           +e`                                                           
      2369 +11. **Health endpoint** (D12) + Docker healthcheck           
      2370 +12. **Cloudflare Tunnel sidecar** (D10) + obsidian-headless c
           +ontainer (D11) in compose                                    
      2371 +13. **End-to-end integration test** — full sync chain on NAS 
      2372 +                                                             
      2373 +**Cross-Component Dependencies:**                            
      2374 +                                                             
      2375 +- D2 (ordering) ↔ D6 (errors): `version_save_failed` must be 
           +raised by coordinator BEFORE file touch                      
      2376 +- D4 (path security) → D6 (errors): `note_path_invalid` raise
           +d exclusively by path helper                                 
      2377 +- D8 (service reuse) may block or fork tool implementation if
           + coupling discovered                                         
      2378 +- D10 (tunnel) + D12 (healthz): healthz routing must bypass O
           +Auth (Cloudflare Access bypass rule on `/healthz` path) OR be
           + exposed on internal-only port                               
      2379 +- D11 (obsidian-headless) is independent of MCP server — runs
           + as peer, not child                                          
      2380 +                                                             
      2381 +**Deferred / Out of Sprint 10 Scope (deferred to Phase 2 per 
           +PRD):**                                                      
      2382 +                                                             
      2383 +- Rate limiting (D-deferred): PRD declares single-user MVP ex
           +clusion                                                      
      2384 +- Monitoring / alerting (D-deferred): PRD Phase 2            
      2385 +- Automated quality audit of note changes (D-deferred): PRD b
           +acklog                                                       
      2386 +- `obsidian_update_note` partial edits (D-deferred): PRD Phas
           +e 2                                                          
      2387 +- Defense-in-depth MCP auth token (D-deferred): PRD explicit 
           +MVP exclusion                                                

● Zapisane. Step 5 — Implementation Patterns & Consistency Rules:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Step 5 — Implementation Patterns. Dla brownfield projektu większość patternów
  jest ustalona w istniejących Sprint 1-6 sekcjach (naming, structure, testing).
   Fokusuję się na patternach specyficznych dla MCP których agenci mogliby
  zaimplementować inaczej.

  Sprint 10 — MCP-Specific Consistency Patterns

  Key Conflict Points Identified (8 obszarów)

  Tool-level patterns (co może zrobić każdy MCP tool inaczej):

  1. Tool naming convention — agent mógłby użyć getArticle / get_article /
  lenie.get / itp.
  2. Parameter naming — articleId vs article_id vs id
  3. Return shape — Pydantic model vs dict vs list
  4. Error raising — raise ValueError vs McpError vs custom exception
  5. Path parameter format — absolute vs relative, with/without leading /
  6. Service invocation — raw SQL vs ORM vs istniejące services
  7. Session lifecycle — one session per server vs per tool call
  8. Diff output format — lista stringów vs single string vs strukturowany
  object

  Proponowana treść do architecture.md

  ## Sprint 10 — Implementation Patterns & Consistency Rules

  ### Pattern Categories Defined

  **Critical conflict points identified:** 8 MCP-specific areas where AI agents
  could diverge without explicit patterns.

  ### Naming Patterns (MCP-specific)

  **Tool naming:**

  - Format: `<scope>_<verb>_<noun>` in `snake_case`
  - Scope is `lenie` or `obsidian` (prefix locks tool to data source)
  - Examples: `lenie_get_article`, `obsidian_write_note`,
  `obsidian_note_history`
  - Tool names are the public API surface (PRD stability contract) — NEVER
  rename without API version bump

  **Tool parameter naming:**

  - `snake_case` for all parameters (Python + JSON-RPC friendly)
  - Common params: `article_uuid: str`, `note_path: str`, `limit: int = 10`,
  `offset: int = 0`
  - Path parameters are ALWAYS vault-relative, NEVER absolute
  - Forbidden: `camelCase` param names (rejected by pattern)

  **Tool return key naming:**

  - `snake_case` keys throughout response payloads
  - Timestamps: ISO 8601 UTC strings (e.g. `"2026-04-13T10:30:00Z"`), never
  epoch integers
  - Null fields: include key with `null` value, don't omit the key
  (predictability for Claude)

  ### Structure Patterns

  **Tool module organization:**

  - One Python module per tool scope: `tools/lenie.py`, `tools/obsidian.py`
  - Each module defines its tools using `@mcp.tool()` decorators, registered at
  module import
  - Shared helpers in `tools/_common.py` (session factory, response builders)
  - NO tool logic outside `tools/` subdirectory

  **Error handling organization:**

  - ALL errors raised via helpers in `backend/mcp_server/errors.py`
  - NEVER raise raw `Exception`, `ValueError`, `FileNotFoundError` from tool
  code — catch at boundary, convert via helpers
  - Pattern: `try: ... except FileNotFoundError: raise_note_not_found(path)`

  **Path security enforcement:**

  - EVERY Obsidian tool begins with `resolved = ensure_within_vault(note_path)`
  - NEVER construct filesystem paths manually in tool code — always via helper
  result
  - Bypass of `ensure_within_vault` is an architectural violation (flagged in
  code review / lint rule)

  ### Format Patterns

  **Tool return shape:**

  - Return plain Python `dict` / `list[dict]` — FastMCP serializes via
  `json.dumps` default encoder
  - Do NOT return Pydantic models from tools (SDK handles serialization
  natively; explicit models add noise)
  - List endpoints return `{"items": [...], "total": N, "limit": L, "offset":
  O}` envelope — NOT bare list
  - Single-item GETs return flat `dict` — NOT wrapped in `{"data": ...}`

  **Error response format:**

  - Raised as `McpError(code=<jsonrpc_code>, message=<human_msg>)` via helpers
  - JSON-RPC code range: `-32001` to `-32006` (one per our 6 error codes;
  mapping frozen in `errors.py`)
  - Human message in Polish (matches Claude conversation language + PRD
  user-facing patterns)

  **Diff format (FR13 / `obsidian_note_history`):**

  - Unified diff as single string (result of
  `"\n".join(difflib.unified_diff(...))`)
  - Include fromfile/tofile labels: `version_<created_at>` /
  `version_<next_created_at>` or `current`
  - Default context lines: 3 (Python difflib default)

  **Pagination parameters:**

  - All list-returning tools accept `limit: int` and `offset: int`
  - Defaults: `limit=10` (except `lenie_unreviewed_articles`: `limit=6` per PRD
  FR1)
  - Max limit enforced: 100 (prevent accidental full-table scans via Claude
  prompts)
  - Returned envelope always includes `total` (full count before pagination)

  ### Communication Patterns

  **Logging:**

  - Python `logging` module, logger name = module `__name__`
  - Log levels:
    - `INFO` — tool invocations: `tool_name`, `user_email` (from Cf header),
  param summary (excluding sensitive content)
    - `WARNING` — orphan version records detected, path traversal attempts
  rejected
    - `ERROR` — unexpected exceptions before conversion to `McpError`
  - Format: structured (key=value or JSON), timestamp UTC
  - NEVER log full article content or note content (privacy, log size)

  **SQLAlchemy session lifecycle:**

  - One session per tool invocation (request-scoped)
  - Pattern: `with session_factory() as session: ...` inside tool function
  - NEVER cache sessions across tool calls
  - Rationale: FastMCP tool calls are stateless (matches D3 stateless_http=True)

  ### Process Patterns

  **Service invocation priority (decision ladder):**

  1. **PREFER:** existing `DocumentService` / `SearchService` methods from 
  `backend/library/`
  2. **IF not covered:** add method to existing service (not new service)
  3. **IF truly new domain:** SQLAlchemy ORM query in tool module via session
  4. **NEVER:** raw SQL strings in MCP tool code (inconsistent with Sprint 9 ORM
   adoption)

  **Write coordination pattern (D2 implementation):**

  ```python
  # Pseudocode for obsidian_write_note
  with session_factory() as session:
      # Phase 1: DB version write
      existing_content = read_file_if_exists(resolved_path)
      version = ObsidianNoteVersion(
          note_path=relative_path,
          content_before=existing_content,
          content_after=new_content,
          user_prompt=user_prompt,
          article_id=article_id,
          changed_by="mcp_server",
      )
      session.add(version)
      try:
          session.commit()
      except SQLAlchemyError as e:
          raise_version_save_failed(e)
      # Phase 2: file write (only after DB commit)
      try:
          resolved_path.write_text(new_content, encoding="utf-8")
      except OSError as e:
          raise_vault_write_failed(e)
      # Phase 3: mark reviewed (optional, separate DB op)
      if mark_as_reviewed and article_id:
          doc_service.mark_reviewed(article_id, session=session)

  Input validation:

  - FastMCP + Pydantic via type hints handles structural validation
  - Domain validation (UUID format, path format) in tool body, raising
  appropriate McpError
  - NEVER silently coerce invalid input — always error with clear message

  Enforcement Guidelines

  All AI Agents MUST:

  - Use tool naming <scope>_<verb>_<noun> with lenie/obsidian scope prefix
  - Raise errors only via helpers in errors.py (never raw exceptions from tools)
  - Wrap every filesystem access with ensure_within_vault()
  - Prefer existing services (DocumentService / SearchService) over new SQL
  - Return plain dict/list, never Pydantic models from tools
  - Include total + limit + offset envelope for list returns
  - Use per-invocation SQLAlchemy session, not global/cached

  Pattern Enforcement:

  - ruff rules in backend/pyproject.toml should include E/F/N for naming
  - Custom code review checklist items:
    - "Does every tools/obsidian/* function call ensure_within_vault before
  filesystem access?"
    - "Are all error raises routed through errors.py helpers?"
    - "Does every write tool follow the 3-phase coordinator pattern?"
  - Pattern violations go to PR reviewers with link to this section

  Pattern Examples

  Good — Lenie tool:

  @mcp.tool()
  def lenie_get_article(article_uuid: str) -> dict:
      """Retrieve full article content and metadata."""
      with session_factory() as session:
          doc_service = DocumentService(session=session)
          article = doc_service.get_by_uuid(article_uuid)
          if article is None:
              raise_article_not_found(article_uuid)
          return {
              "uuid": article.uuid,
              "title": article.title,
              "content_markdown": article.content_markdown,
              "source": article.source,
              "language": article.language,
              "date": article.created_at.isoformat() + "Z",
              "user_note": article.user_note,
              "obsidian_note_paths": article.obsidian_note_paths or [],
          }

  Good — Obsidian tool with path security:

  @mcp.tool()
  def obsidian_read_note(note_path: str) -> dict:
      """Read full content of a note within 02-wiedza/."""
      resolved = ensure_within_vault(note_path)
      if not resolved.exists():
          raise_note_not_found(note_path)
      return {
          "path": note_path,
          "content": resolved.read_text(encoding="utf-8"),
          "modified_at": datetime.fromtimestamp(
              resolved.stat().st_mtime, tz=UTC
          ).isoformat(),
      }

  Anti-pattern — raw exception leak:

  # ❌ WRONG: exception leaks to MCP transport as generic error
  @mcp.tool()
  def obsidian_read_note(note_path: str) -> dict:
      full_path = Path(VAULT_ROOT) / note_path  # ❌ no path security
      return {"content": full_path.read_text()}  # ❌ FileNotFoundError leaks

  Anti-pattern — Pydantic return model:

  # ❌ WRONG: Pydantic model adds serialization noise, inconsistent with pattern
  class ArticleResponse(BaseModel):
      uuid: str
      title: str

  @mcp.tool()
  def lenie_get_article(article_uuid: str) -> ArticleResponse:  # ❌ return dict
   instead
      ...

  Anti-pattern — raw SQL:

  # ❌ WRONG: raw SQL bypasses Sprint 9 ORM adoption
  @mcp.tool()
  def lenie_search(query: str) -> dict:
      rows = session.execute(f"SELECT * FROM web_documents WHERE title LIKE 
  '%{query}%'")  # ❌ SQL injection + raw SQL

  **[A]** Advanced Elicitation — pogłębić konkretne patterns (np. logging
  format, session lifecycle edge cases)

   na tool ergonomics)

  Boundaries)

      2460 +                                                             
      2461 +**Pagination parameters:**                                   
      2462 +                                                             
      2463 +- All list-returning tools accept `limit: int` and `offset: i
           +nt`                                                          
      2464 +- Defaults: `limit=10` (except `lenie_unreviewed_articles`: `
           +limit=6` per PRD FR1)                                        
      2465 +- Max limit enforced: 100 (prevent accidental full-table scan
           +s via Claude prompts)                                        
      2466 +- Returned envelope always includes `total` (full count befor
           +e pagination)                                                
      2467 +                                                             
      2468 +### Communication Patterns                                   
      2469 +                                                             
      2470 +**Logging:**                                                 
      2471 +                                                             
      2472 +- Python `logging` module, logger name = module `__name__`   
      2473 +- Log levels:                                                
      2474 +  - `INFO` — tool invocations: `tool_name`, `user_email` (fro
           +m Cf header), param summary (excluding sensitive content)    
      2475 +  - `WARNING` — orphan version records detected, path travers
           +al attempts rejected                                         
      2476 +  - `ERROR` — unexpected exceptions before conversion to `Mcp
           +Error`                                                       
      2477 +- Format: structured (key=value or JSON), timestamp UTC      
      2478 +- NEVER log full article content or note content (privacy, lo
           +g size)                                                      
      2479 +                                                             
      2480 +**SQLAlchemy session lifecycle:**                            
      2481 +                                                             
      2482 +- One session per tool invocation (request-scoped)           
      2483 +- Pattern: `with session_factory() as session: ...` inside to
           +ol function                                                  
      2484 +- NEVER cache sessions across tool calls                     
      2485 +- Rationale: FastMCP tool calls are stateless (matches D3 `st
           +ateless_http=True`)                                          
      2486 +                                                             
      2487 +### Process Patterns                                         
      2488 +                                                             
      2489 +**Service invocation priority (decision ladder):**           
      2490 +                                                             
      2491 +1. **PREFER:** existing `DocumentService` / `SearchService` m
           +ethods from `backend/library/`                               
      2492 +2. **IF not covered:** add method to existing service (not ne
           +w service)                                                   
      2493 +3. **IF truly new domain:** SQLAlchemy ORM query in tool modu
           +le via session                                               
      2494 +4. **NEVER:** raw SQL strings in MCP tool code (inconsistent 
           +with Sprint 9 ORM adoption)                                  
      2495 +                                                             
      2496 +**Write coordination pattern (D2 implementation):**          
      2497 +                                                             
      2498 +```python                                                    
      2499 +# Pseudocode for obsidian_write_note                         
      2500 +with session_factory() as session:                           
      2501 +    # Phase 1: DB version write                              
      2502 +    existing_content = read_file_if_exists(resolved_path)    
      2503 +    version = ObsidianNoteVersion(                           
      2504 +        note_path=relative_path,                             
      2505 +        content_before=existing_content,                     
      2506 +        content_after=new_content,                           
      2507 +        user_prompt=user_prompt,                             
      2508 +        article_id=article_id,                               
      2509 +        changed_by="mcp_server",                             
      2510 +    )                                                        
      2511 +    session.add(version)                                     
      2512 +    try:                                                     
      2513 +        session.commit()                                     
      2514 +    except SQLAlchemyError as e:                             
      2515 +        raise_version_save_failed(e)                         
      2516 +    # Phase 2: file write (only after DB commit)             
      2517 +    try:                                                     
      2518 +        resolved_path.write_text(new_content, encoding="utf-8
           +")                                                           
      2519 +    except OSError as e:                                     
      2520 +        raise_vault_write_failed(e)                          
      2521 +    # Phase 3: mark reviewed (optional, separate DB op)      
      2522 +    if mark_as_reviewed and article_id:                      
      2523 +        doc_service.mark_reviewed(article_id, session=session
           +)                                                            
      2524 +```                                                          
      2525 +                                                             
      2526 +**Input validation:**                                        
      2527 +                                                             
      2528 +- FastMCP + Pydantic via type hints handles structural valida
           +tion                                                         
      2529 +- Domain validation (UUID format, path format) in tool body, 
           +raising appropriate `McpError`                               
      2530 +- NEVER silently coerce invalid input — always error with cle
           +ar message                                                   
      2531 +                                                             
      2532 +### Enforcement Guidelines                                   
      2533 +                                                             
      2534 +**All AI Agents MUST:**                                      
      2535 +                                                             
      2536 +- Use tool naming `<scope>_<verb>_<noun>` with `lenie`/`obsid
           +ian` scope prefix                                            
      2537 +- Raise errors only via helpers in `errors.py` (never raw exc
           +eptions from tools)                                          
      2538 +- Wrap every filesystem access with `ensure_within_vault()`  
      2539 +- Prefer existing services (`DocumentService` / `SearchServic
           +e`) over new SQL                                             
      2540 +- Return plain `dict`/`list`, never Pydantic models from tool
           +s                                                            
      2541 +- Include `total` + `limit` + `offset` envelope for list retu
           +rns                                                          
      2542 +- Use per-invocation SQLAlchemy session, not global/cached   
      2543 +                                                             
      2544 +**Pattern Enforcement:**                                     
      2545 +                                                             
      2546 +- `ruff` rules in `backend/pyproject.toml` should include E/F
           +/N for naming                                                
      2547 +- Custom code review checklist items:                        
      2548 +  - "Does every `tools/obsidian/*` function call `ensure_with
           +in_vault` before filesystem access?"                         
      2549 +  - "Are all error raises routed through `errors.py` helpers?
           +"                                                            
      2550 +  - "Does every write tool follow the 3-phase coordinator pat
           +tern?"                                                       
      2551 +- Pattern violations go to PR reviewers with link to this sec
           +tion                                                         
      2552 +                                                             
      2553 +### Pattern Examples                                         
      2554 +                                                             
      2555 +**Good — Lenie tool:**                                       
      2556 +                                                             
      2557 +```python                                                    
      2558 +@mcp.tool()                                                  
      2559 +def lenie_get_article(article_uuid: str) -> dict:            
      2560 +    """Retrieve full article content and metadata."""        
      2561 +    with session_factory() as session:                       
      2562 +        doc_service = DocumentService(session=session)       
      2563 +        article = doc_service.get_by_uuid(article_uuid)      
      2564 +        if article is None:                                  
      2565 +            raise_article_not_found(article_uuid)            
      2566 +        return {                                             
      2567 +            "uuid": article.uuid,                            
      2568 +            "title": article.title,                          
      2569 +            "content_markdown": article.content_markdown,    
      2570 +            "source": article.source,                        
      2571 +            "language": article.language,                    
      2572 +            "date": article.created_at.isoformat() + "Z",    
      2573 +            "user_note": article.user_note,                  
      2574 +            "obsidian_note_paths": article.obsidian_note_path
           +s or [],                                                     
      2575 +        }                                                    
      2576 +```                                                          
      2577 +                                                             
      2578 +**Good — Obsidian tool with path security:**                 
      2579 +                                                             
      2580 +```python                                                    
      2581 +@mcp.tool()                                                  
      2582 +def obsidian_read_note(note_path: str) -> dict:              
      2583 +    """Read full content of a note within 02-wiedza/."""     
      2584 +    resolved = ensure_within_vault(note_path)                
      2585 +    if not resolved.exists():                                
      2586 +        raise_note_not_found(note_path)                      
      2587 +    return {                                                 
      2588 +        "path": note_path,                                   
      2589 +        "content": resolved.read_text(encoding="utf-8"),     
      2590 +        "modified_at": datetime.fromtimestamp(               
      2591 +            resolved.stat().st_mtime, tz=UTC                 
      2592 +        ).isoformat(),                                       
      2593 +    }                                                        
      2594 +```                                                          
      2595 +                                                             
      2596 +**Anti-pattern — raw exception leak:**                       
      2597 +                                                             
      2598 +```python                                                    
      2599 +# WRONG: exception leaks to MCP transport as generic error   
      2600 +@mcp.tool()                                                  
      2601 +def obsidian_read_note(note_path: str) -> dict:              
      2602 +    full_path = Path(VAULT_ROOT) / note_path  # no path secur
           +ity                                                          
      2603 +    return {"content": full_path.read_text()}  # FileNotFound
           +Error leaks                                                  
      2604 +```                                                          
      2605 +                                                             
      2606 +**Anti-pattern — Pydantic return model:**                    
      2607 +                                                             
      2608 +```python                                                    
      2609 +# WRONG: Pydantic model adds serialization noise, inconsisten
           +t with pattern                                               
      2610 +class ArticleResponse(BaseModel):                            
      2611 +    uuid: str                                                
      2612 +    title: str                                               
      2613 +                                                             
      2614 +@mcp.tool()                                                  
      2615 +def lenie_get_article(article_uuid: str) -> ArticleResponse: 
           + # return dict instead                                       
      2616 +    ...                                                      
      2617 +```                                                          
      2618 +                                                             
      2619 +**Anti-pattern — raw SQL:**                                  
      2620 +                                                             
      2621 +```python                                                    
      2622 +# WRONG: raw SQL bypasses Sprint 9 ORM adoption; SQL injectio
           +n risk                                                       
      2623 +@mcp.tool()                                                  
      2624 +def lenie_search(query: str) -> dict:                        
      2625 +    rows = session.execute(f"SELECT * FROM web_documents WHER
           +E title LIKE '%{query}%'")                                   
      2626 +```

  ## Sprint 10 — Project Structure & Boundaries

  ### Scope of this Section

  **Brownfield sprint — only NEW footprint documented.** Existing project
  structure (backend layout, frontend apps, docs organization, testing
  conventions) remains governed by Sprint 1-6 architecture sections. This
  section adds the MCP server subtree + infrastructure touchpoints.
